<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">BH_A006 has a nontrivial payload execution scheme, which can vary at the initial stages in different samples. Let&#x27;s consider it using the example of one of the malicious files.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-1" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 0. Loading DLL from the overlay</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">SHA-256: 1e725f1fe67d1a596c9677df69ef5b1b2c29903e84d7b08284f0a767aedcc097</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The source sample is an executable file that uses the MFC library. It extracts the contents of the overlay, decrypts itswith XOR with the 0xA0 key, and reflectively loads the resulting DLL into memory.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-2" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 1. DLL dropper</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">SHA-256: 8bf3df654459b1b8f553ad9a0770058fd2c31262f38f2e8ba12943f813200a4d</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">extracts the following files:</p>
<ul class="listStyles_list__w6p69 listStyles_ul__CFFG0 weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA margin_xs__lb5TS">
<li>C:\ProgramData\resmon.resmoncfg</li>
<li>C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SbieIni.dat (install32.dat)</li>
<li>C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SbieDll.dll</li>
<li>C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SandboxieBITS.exe</li>
</ul>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">After that, there is a check for write permission to the system folder. For this, the dropper tries to create a file in it with the name format: wmkawe_%d.data. The content is the Stupid Japanese string.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">If there is no permission, and the system is 64-bit, two additional files are extracted:</p>
<ul class="listStyles_list__w6p69 listStyles_ul__CFFG0 weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA margin_xs__lb5TS">
<li>C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie.dll (install64.dll)</li>
<li>C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie.dat (install64.dat)</li>
</ul>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The names given in parentheses are not used, but are present in the code. Apparently, they were left there from another version of the dropper.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">All the files are contained in the data section in packaged form; a variant of the LZMA algorithm is used for compression. This compression method is also used in further stages of the malware operation. Further in the section, unless otherwise indicated, we will refer to this algorithm.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Depending on the available permissions and the OS bitness, the dropper starts one of the chains to bypass the UAC:</p>
<ul class="listStyles_list__w6p69 listStyles_ul__CFFG0 weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA margin_xs__lb5TS">
<li>(x32) C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SandboxieBITS.exe ByPassUAC</li>
<li>(x64) rundll32.exe C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SbieMsg.dll,installsvc ByPassUAC</li>
</ul>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Or it immediately proceeds to the execution of the next stage:<br/>
C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SandboxieBITS.exe InsertS</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">In all three cases, the file %tmp%\delself.bat is created, which contains commands for self-removal.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Note that it is not the first time researchers have encountered this sample. Another variant of the MFC loader (<a class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="#id3-6-1" href="#id3-6-1">stage 0</a>) containing the same dropper was mentioned by ESET in the <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://www.welivesecurity.com/2021/02/01/operation-nightscout-supply-chain-attack-online-gaming-asia/" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://www.welivesecurity.com/2021/02/01/operation-nightscout-supply-chain-attack-online-gaming-asia/">Operation NightScout</a> report, and then <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://blog.vincss.net/2021/02/re020-elephantrat-kunming-version-our-latest-discovered-RAT-of-Panda.html" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://blog.vincss.net/2021/02/re020-elephantrat-kunming-version-our-latest-discovered-RAT-of-Panda.html">studied</a> in detail by our colleagues from VinCSS.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-3" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 2. .dat loader (SbieDll.dll / SbieMsg.dll)</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Regardless of the command run by the DLL dropper, execution jumps to one of the extracted DLL libraries. In the case of a 32-bit version, a legitimate component of the <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandboxie" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandboxie">Sandboxie</a> utility, which is vulnerable to DLL side-loading, is used for this.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image27.png" alt="Figure 27. Loading and running the shellcode in SbieDll.dll"/>
<figcaption>Figure 27. Loading and running the shellcode in SbieDll.dll</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The code in the 32-bit and 64-bit versions of the libraries is almost identical and downloads the corresponding .dat file, decrypts its contents, and executes it. For decryption, XOR is used with the byte sequence: 00, 01, 02, ... FF, 00, 01, ... Just as in the code of the previous stage, here you can see alternative paths to .dat files that are not used during operation.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-4" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 3. Shellcode .dat and DLL</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The shellcode is a reflective DLL library loader, which is located in its body immediately after the loading function. In this case, the library functionality differs significantly in shellcode versions with different bitness.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.1 ByPassUAC (x64)</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b id="stage3-1-1">Stage 3.1.1 Intermediate DLL</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The 64-bit version is only responsible for implementing the UAC bypass. To perform this task, it extracts another DLL from itself into memory and transfers control to it. Reflective loading is performed again using a shellcode, which is predecrypted with XOR using the 0x97 key. The shellcode is not autonomous: in addition to the buffer with the PE file, pointers to the necessary functions, such as GetProcAddress and LoadLibraryA, are passed to it.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image28.png" alt="Figure 28. Decryption and execution of the shellcode for reflective loading"/>
<figcaption>Figure 28. Decryption and execution of the shellcode for reflective loading</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.1.2 DLL with UAC bypass implementation</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The DLL contains the path to the PDB file: e:\F35-F22\昆明版本\ElephantRat\nwsapagent\Bin\ByPassUAC64.pdb.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image29.png" alt="Figure 29. Choosing a UAC bypass method"/>
<figcaption>Figure 29. Choosing a UAC bypass method</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The UAC bypass method used depends on the presence in the system of the avp.exe process (a component of Kaspersky antivirus products) and on the system version. In total, three well-known methods using <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="http://blog.sevagas.com/?Yet-another-sdclt-UAC-bypass" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="http://blog.sevagas.com/?Yet-another-sdclt-UAC-bypass">sdclt.exe</a>, a <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://offsec.almond.consulting/UAC-bypass-dotnet.html" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://offsec.almond.consulting/UAC-bypass-dotnet.html">.NET library</a>, and <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://medium.com/tenable-techblog/uac-bypass-by-mocking-trusted-directories-24a96675f6e" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://medium.com/tenable-techblog/uac-bypass-by-mocking-trusted-directories-24a96675f6e">mocking trusted directories</a> have been implemented.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">If the bypass is successfully implemented using any of the methods, the previously encountered command C:\ProgramData\Sandboxie\SandboxieBITS.exe InsertS is run.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.2. ByPassUAC / InstallS (x32)</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b id="stage3-2-1">Stage 3.2.1. Intermediate DLL</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The 32-bit version of the DLL, which is located in the corresponding DAT file, is obfuscated using an unknown protector.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image30.png" alt="Figure 30. The entry point in the obfuscated PE file"/>
<figcaption>Figure 30. The entry point in the obfuscated PE file</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">In the data section of this DLL, there is a compressed shellcode that is decompressed and gains control.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.2.2. Decompression shellcode</b></p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image31.png" alt="Figure 31. Passing arguments to the function via the return address"/>
<figcaption>Figure 31. Passing arguments to the function via the return address</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The shellcode starts with calling the sub_20F function, which takes three arguments: a hash on behalf of VirtualAlloc, the size of the buffer to decompress, and a pointer to the data. The arguments are written immediately after the call statement, and the called function accesses them using an offset relative to the return address.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The sub_20F function gets a pointer to the VirtualAlloc function, for which it finds the kernelbase.dll library in the list of loaded modules (which is always assumed to be in second place on the InInitializationOrderModuleList list) and iterates its export table using a hash to find the required function. Then a buffer of the size specified in the arguments with RWX rights is allocated, and the compressed data is unpacked into it. In this case, compression is done with the NRV family algorithm from the <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="http://www.oberhumer.com/opensource/ucl/" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="http://www.oberhumer.com/opensource/ucl/">UCL library</a> (used in the UPX packer). The data is another shellcode to which control is transferred.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.2.3. Relocation shellcode</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The main part of the next shellcode is the contents of data and code sections, apparently extracted from some PE file. To launch correctly at the beginning of its operation, the shellcode performs address correction (relocation). The parameters necessary for it are transmitted in the same way as the previous shellcode using the return address. The relocation is performed relative to the standard base address 0x401000. After its completion, control is transferred to the address of the entry point specified in the parameters (as an offset relative to the end of the relocation table).</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image32.png" alt="Figure 32. Parameters of the relocation shellcode"/>
<figcaption>Figure 32. Parameters of the relocation shellcode</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA"><b>Stage 3.2.4. Installer in shellcode format</b></p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The main function of the installer loads the WinAPI functions necessary for operation, after which it can perform the operation specified in the command line.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image33.png" alt="Figure 33. Code fragment of the shellcode installer"/>
<figcaption>Figure 33. Code fragment of the shellcode installer</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The following commands are supported:</p>
<ul class="listStyles_list__w6p69 listStyles_ul__CFFG0 weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA margin_xs__lb5TS">
<li>InsertS: create a service named Network Service. The name of the current module with the runsvc parameter is specified as the launch path. If there are no avp.exe processes in the list, the service is launched immediately.</li>
<li><p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Runsvc: delete all auxiliary files and folders that could be used in the UAC bypass. Decompressing the next-stage shellcode, creating an svchost.exe process, and injecting the decompressed shellcode.
Interestingly, in the code for impersonation and starting the svchost.exe process, a special check has been implemented only for the Russian language, which indicates an orientation to Russian-language OS versions.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image34.png" alt="Figure 34. Special processing for the Russian-language version of the system"/>
<figcaption>Figure 34. Special processing for the Russian-language version of the system</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">In addition, a separate thread is created that checks for Global\MYKERNELDLLMAPPING06 mapping every 50 seconds. In case of its absence in the system, the creation of svchost.exe and shellcode injection are repeated.</p>
</li>
<li>ByPassUAC: works completely similar to the 64-bit version (<a class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="#stage3-1-1" href="#stage3-1-1">stage 3.1.1</a>)—it decompresses the DLL with the implementation of UAC bypass methods and transfers control to it.</li>
<li>Memload: there is a MemLoadServer debug message in the code. Decompresses the next-stage shellcode and runs it directly in the current process.</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="id3-6-5" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 4. MemLoadLibrary</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The fourth stage has a previously encountered format: the decompression shellcode extracts the relocation shellcode, which in turn executes the main code (obtained from the PE file). The main code in this case is small in volume and is responsible for decompressing and reflectively loading the DLL into memory. The reflective loader is implemented in the form of an XOR-encrypted shellcode, as in <a class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="#stage3-1-1" href="#stage3-1-1">stage 3.1.1</a>. After loading the library, control is transferred to the exported Online function.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image35.png" alt="Figure 35. Decompressing the DLL and starting the Online export"/>
<figcaption>Figure 35. Decompressing the DLL and starting the Online export</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The DLL is again just an intermediate loader and runs another shellcode.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image36.png" alt="Figure 36. Online function code"/>
<figcaption>Figure 36. Online function code</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The new shellcode is an unpacking shellcode, and stage 4 is repeated exactly, right up to calling the Online function from the latest DLL library.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-6" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Stage 5. Payload</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">It is a backdoor partially obfuscated with the help of a previously encountered packer (<a class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="#stage3-2-1" href="#stage3-2-1">stage 3.2.1</a>), which is based on the Gh0st trojan code.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Interestingly, the signature of network packets (Gh0st in the original) in this version is generated and checked in a special way. In a 4-byte value, only the lowest bit of each byte carries the payload, the remaining bits are random. The lower bits must satisfy a set of logical relations involving the lower bits of the magic constant 0x31230C0. Note that a similar algorithm for checking these relations using the same constant can be found in loaders of .dat files (<a class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="#id3-6-3" href="#id3-6-3">stage 2</a>), but the result of its operation is not used there.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image37.png" alt="Figure 37. Generating a signature in the constructor of the CClientSocket class"/>
<figcaption>Figure 37. Generating a signature in the constructor of the CClientSocket class</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The library has the export name BH_A006_SRV.dll, and in the PE file overlay, you can find the corresponding PDB path:</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">D:\005（fastapp f35 20181009）\nwsapagent\KernelTrjoan\BH_A006_SRV\BH_A006_SRV\Debug\BH_A006_SRV.pdb</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">We managed to find a sample of the malware (57d4c08ce9a45798cd9b0cf08c933e26ffa964101dcafb1640d1df19c223e738), which has a similar obfuscation and an identical algorithm for generating a network signature, and contains the name BH_A006_SRV.dll. This sample was uploaded to VirusTotal in 2015.</p>
<h4 id="id3-6-7" class="break-words size_xs__89FKN color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Connection with 9002 RAT</h4>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">In studying the execution chain of the BH_A006 backdoor, it turned out that the technique used for converting a PE file into an autonomous compressed shellcode is not unique. Similar decompression and relocation shellcodes, as well as the procedure for loading WinAPI functions, are present in instances of the 9002 RAT malware. For example, they can be found in the sample 52374f68d1e43f1ca6cd04e5816999ba45c4e42eb0641874be25808c9fe15005 from the <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/research/18/h/supply-chain-attack-operation-red-signature-targets-south-korean-organizations.html" class="linkStyles_links-gray__auxKT weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_links-gray__IEMoh linkStyles_underlined__4E3jf" title="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/research/18/h/supply-chain-attack-operation-red-signature-targets-south-korean-organizations.html">Trend Micro report</a> on attacks on South Korean companies—one of the last mentions of this malware.</p>
<h3 id="id3-7" class="break-words size_s__3_Wdt color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Deed RAT</h3>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Another type of previously unknown malware, which we found in a single instance in our client&#x27;s infrastructure, is a modular backdoor. Based on the value of the signature used in the header of its modules, we named it Deed RAT.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The Deed RAT control server ftp.microft.dynssl.com is directly connected to the infrastructure of the Space Pirates group. Another similarity can be found in one of the code features: the [xor 0xBB, sub 0x1] operations are used to encrypt the shellcode in the same way as in the part of PlugX samples.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The payload execution scheme resembles the standard method that PlugX uses: a legitimate EXE file signed by Trend Micro loads a malicious library TmDbgLog.dll, which, in turn, runs the encrypted shellcode from the file PTWD.tmp.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">However, an interesting method of transferring control to the shellcode is used: at the time of loading, the library modifies the executable file so that after returning control to the EXE file, the FreeLibrary function is immediately called for it. Having regained control at the time of unloading, the library modifies the executable file again, writing assembly instructions for calling the shellcode to it—they will be executed immediately after returning from FreeLibrary.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The shellcode is the loader of the main module, which is located in compressed and encrypted form after the loading code. The module has a special structure and uses techniques borrowed from PE files. In particular, the module has three &quot;sections&quot; with different access rights and a relocation table completely similar to the one used in PE format.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The decrypted module consists of a header starting with the signature 0xDEED4554 and a main data block compressed with LZNT1, which contains section data and a relocation table. For each of the sections, the header indicates its actual size and the size in memory, which is aligned to the 0x1000 boundary. The header structure looks as follows:</p>
<div class="bg-skin-content-general-reversed laptop:rounded-xl rounded-lg py-8 pl-5 pr-8 text-[#ABB2BF] HtmlBlock_code__Ng4fC"><div class="pr-15 relative flex gap-5"><pre class="w-full whitespace-pre-wrap break-words"><div class="code">struct SectionHeader{
    _DWORD VirtualSize;
    _DWORD SizeOfRawData;
};

struct ModuleHeader{
    _DWORD Signature; // 0xDEED4554
    _DWORD ModuleId;
    _DWORD EntryPoint;
    _DWORD OriginalBase;
    _DWORD AbsoluteOffset; // 0x1000
    SectionHeader Sections[3];
    _DWORD Unknown;
};</div></pre><div class="absolute bottom-0 right-0" data-theme-direction="reversed"><button type="button" class="IconButton_icon__uMEG7 IconButton_sm__bK6zi IconButton_outlined__kMeaW"><div class="Icon_icon__IyoOP Icon_sm__5FkXp"><svg role="img" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewBox="0 0 20 20" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none"><path stroke="currentColor" d="M6 3a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h8a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v10a2 2 0 0 1-2 2H8a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V3Z"></path><path stroke="currentColor" d="M14 17a2 2 0 0 1-2 2H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V7a2 2 0 0 1 2-2"></path></svg></div></button></div></div></div>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">During operation, the loader allocates the necessary memory area, copies each of the sections into it (taking into account its size in memory), and performs address configuration (relocation). The first of the sections contains executable code, and RX permissions are set for its memory area, the other sections have RW permissions. After loading the sections, the module entry point specified in the header gain control.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The main backdoor module has the identifier 0x20 and is responsible for loading and managing plugins that implement various functions. In its data section, there are eight encrypted plugins that are initialized at the beginning of operation:</p>
<div class="table-container"><table class="table-article">
<thead>
<tr>
<th>ID</th>
<th>Name</th>
<th>Description</th>
<th>Network commands</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>0x30</td>
<td>Startup</td>
<td>A plugin that implements the malware startup algorithm</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x40</td>
<td>Config</td>
<td>A plugin that handles the configuration</td>
<td>0x40: transferring the configuration to C2<br/>
0x41: receiving a new configuration from C2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0xA0</td>
<td>Install</td>
<td>A plugin responsible for persistence on the infected computer. Persistence can be achieved through the mechanism of services and through the registry (the key is set by the configuration)</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0xB0</td>
<td>Inject</td>
<td>A plugin that implements code injection into a given process (determined by the configuration)</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x60</td>
<td>Network</td>
<td>A plugin that manages network interaction</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x70</td>
<td>NetSocket</td>
<td>A plugin that implements various types of connectors for network interaction</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x50</td>
<td>Plugin</td>
<td>A plugin that implements registry monitoring for the appearance of new plugins in it and their loading</td>
<td>0x50: collecting information about plugins<br/>
0x51: adding a plugin to the registry and launching it<br/>
0x52: removing the plugin from the registry and memory</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x90</td>
<td>NetProxy</td>
<td>A plugin that manages information about available proxy servers. It has a built-in sniffer for automatic detection of proxies used by the infected computer</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></div>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Unlike the main module, an algorithm based on Salsa20 is used to encrypt plugins. Among the modifications is a custom constant for the key extension, equal to arbitraryconstat. The structure of the decrypted plugin completely copies the structure of the main module, and a similar algorithm is used to load it.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Each plugin implements five service operations that are implemented at its entry point:</p>
<ol class="listStyles_list__w6p69 listStyles_ol__ZnTfe weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA margin_xs__lb5TS">
<li>Initialization.</li>
<li>Obtaining the numeric ID of the plugin.</li>
<li>Obtaining the plugin name.</li>
<li>Obtaining a link to the structure with the plugin&#x27;s API functions.</li>
<li>Resource deallocation.</li>
</ol>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image38.png" alt="Figure 38. Entry point of the Config plugin"/>
<figcaption>Figure 38. Entry point of the Config plugin</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The useful functionality of the plugin is available through the structure with its API functions. Among them, there may be a dispatcher function responsible for processing network commands that the plugin supports. The main module also has an API that allows you to access other plugins and implements auxiliary functions, such as encryption or access to the registry.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">One interesting feature of the backdoor is the pseudorandom generation of various kinds of strings—registry keys, names of mutexes and pipes, and command-line arguments. A string of the required length is created on the basis of a seed, which is generated using the numeric identifier of the string and the serial number of the system volume. As a result, each of the infected computers uses its own unique set of string constants.</p>
<figure>
<img src="https://pt-corp.storage.yandexcloud.net/upload/corporate/ww-en/images/esc/article_333388/image39.png" alt="Figure 39. ID generation algorithm"/>
<figcaption>Figure 39. ID generation algorithm</figcaption>
</figure>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The backdoor stores all the necessary data in the registry key [HKLM|HKCU]\Software\Microsoft\. For each type of information, it creates its own subkey, the name of which is obtained using the string generator described above. To get all the keys that the backdoor can use, we implemented a script in Python that accepts the serial number of the volume and reproduces the operation of the generator.</p>

<div class="accordion">
    <div class="accordion__item accordionList">
        <!-- -->
        <div class="accordion__content accordionHideList">
            <div class="accordion__inner">
                <article>
                    <div class="bg-skin-content-general-reversed laptop:rounded-xl rounded-lg py-8 pl-5 pr-8 text-[#ABB2BF] HtmlBlock_code__Ng4fC"><div class="pr-15 relative flex gap-5"><pre class="w-full whitespace-pre-wrap break-words">
                      <div class="code">
import click


def rshift(val, n):
    s = val &amp; 0x80000000
    for i in range(0,n):
        val &gt;&gt;= 1
        val |= s
    return val


def generator(volume_number, seed, length):
    gr_seed = (volume_number + seed + 0x1000193) &amp; 0xffffffff
    r = []
    for i in range(length):
        r1 = (gr_seed * 0x2001) &amp; 0xffffffff
        r2 = rshift(r1, 7)
        r3 = r2 ^ r1
        r4 = (r3 * 9) &amp; 0xffffffff
        r5 = rshift(r4, 17)
        r6 = r4 ^ r5
        r7 = (r6 * 33) &amp; 0xffffffff
        r.append(((r7 &amp; 0xffff) % 26) + 0x41)
        gr_seed = r7 
    
    return bytes(r).decode(&#x27;utf-8&#x27;)

@click.command()
@click.argument(&quot;VOLUME_NUMBER&quot;)
def main(volume_number):
    try:
        serial_number = int(volume_number, 16)
    except ValueError:
        print(&quot;[~] Invalid Volume number&quot;)
        return 

    registry_key_1 = generator(serial_number, 0xC4DA8B2F, 6)

    registry_key_2 = generator(serial_number, 0x7BD90AA1, 10)
    registry_key_3 = generator(serial_number, 0xF7BBC23F, 10)

    registry_key_4 = generator(serial_number, 0xDF12A5B2, 8)
    registry_key_5 = generator(serial_number, 0x6EB208A4, 9)

    registry_key_6 = generator(serial_number, 0xDE8765CB, 8)
    registry_key_7 = generator(serial_number, 0x6D3C218A, 8)

    registry_key_8 = generator(serial_number, 0x78D3BC22, 8)
    registry_key_9 = generator(serial_number, 0xD53BCA90, 10)

    registry_key_11 = generator(serial_number, 0x4FD82CB4, 8)
    registry_key_13 = generator(serial_number, 0xDCBC5D23, 8)

    registry_key_10 = generator(serial_number, 0xE2C7BA56, 15)
    
    registry_key_12 = generator(serial_number, 0x8BD43C12, 8)

    print(f&quot;[+] Plugin monitor registry key: [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_1}&quot;)
    print(f&quot;[+] Executable path: [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_3}; ValueName: {registry_key_2}&quot;)
    print(f&quot;[+] Machine ID: [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_5}; ValueName: {registry_key_4}&quot;)
    print(f&quot;[+] Shellcode for injection: [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_6}; ValueName: {registry_key_7}&quot;)
    print(f&quot;[+] Proxies: [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_9}; ValueName: {registry_key_8}&quot;)
    print(f&quot;[+] Config : [HKCU|HKLM]\\Software\\Microsoft\\{registry_key_11}; ValueName: {registry_key_13}&quot;)

if __name__ == &quot;__main__&quot;:
    main()
                      </div>
                    </pre><div class="absolute bottom-0 right-0" data-theme-direction="reversed"><button type="button" class="IconButton_icon__uMEG7 IconButton_sm__bK6zi IconButton_outlined__kMeaW"><div class="Icon_icon__IyoOP Icon_sm__5FkXp"><svg role="img" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewBox="0 0 20 20" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none"><path stroke="currentColor" d="M6 3a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h8a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v10a2 2 0 0 1-2 2H8a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V3Z"></path><path stroke="currentColor" d="M14 17a2 2 0 0 1-2 2H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V7a2 2 0 0 1 2-2"></path></svg></div></button></div></div></div>
                </article>
            </div>
        </div>
    </div>
</div>

<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The Network plugin is responsible for the algorithm of interaction with the control server. It extracts the C2 address as a URL string from the configuration and, depending on the scheme specified in it, selects one of the connectors available in the NetSocket plugin. All of them implement a common interface for uniformly receiving and transmitting network messages. Before sending, messages are compressed using the LZNT1 algorithm and encrypted with a modified Salsa20 using a random key.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">To resolve the domain of the control server, the backdoor consistently uses DNS over HTTPS and the usual DNS servers specified in the configuration (public servers of Google and other providers), before resorting to the standard mechanism. This gives the malware the opportunity to hide the C2 domain from network traffic inspection tools.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Supported connection protocols include TCP, TLS, HTTP, HTTPS, UDP, and DNS.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The REUSEPORT option is available for TCP—specifying it leads to prebinding of the socket with which the connection to C2 is established. Binding is performed on the largest free port in the range of system (well-known) ports. The ports are checked starting from 1022 in descending order. Apparently, this technique is implemented to bypass security measures and disguise traffic as system network services.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The backdoor also provides for the possibility of obtaining a new C2 over HTTP. To do this, a web page can be used, the address of which is specified in the configuration with the URL:// scheme. After the page loads, its body is searched for the agmsy4 and ciou0 substrings, which indicate the beginning and end of the string with the control server. This string is encoded using base16 (hex) with the abcghimnostuyz0456 alphabet and is processed similarly to the address from the configuration.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">TCP/TLS and HTTP/HTTPS connectors support connection via a proxy server, which can be obtained using the NetProxy plugin. The plugin has its own proxy storage, which is located in the registry and can be filled with values from the configuration, system proxies, and data from installed browsers (Chrome, Opera, and Firefox). In addition, the plugin has the functionality of a built-in sniffer that listens to the traffic of the infected computer using a raw socket. If the sniffer detects an attempt to connect to a proxy server (SOCKS4, SOCKS5, or HTTP) in the outgoing packet, it saves information about it in the storage.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">Before connecting to the control server, the backdoor checks the schedule: up to four entries can be specified in its configuration, containing the days of the week and the hours during which the connection is prohibited.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">After the connection is established, the backdoor can execute the following commands:</p>
<div class="table-container"><table class="table-article">
<thead>
<tr>
<th>ID</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>0x210</td>
<td>Collect information about the system</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x211</td>
<td>Creation of a separate connection to work with plugins</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x212</td>
<td>Self-removal</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x213</td>
<td>Empty command (ping)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x214</td>
<td>Connection deactivation</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x215</td>
<td>Update of the shellcode for the injection, which is stored in the registry</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>0x216</td>
<td>Update of the main shellcode on the disk. All plugins stored in the registry are deleted</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></div>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">If a command is received that is not on the list above, it is assumed that it is a network command of one of the plugins. Its ID is determined by applying the mask 0xFFF0 to the command ID. If the plugin is not available locally, it is preloaded from C2 and saved in the registry.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">On the computer infected with Deed RAT, we were able to detect a single plugin obtained dynamically from the control server. It is called Shell, and its ID is 0x270. Shell supports two network commands (0x270 and 0x271); each of them starts the specified process and redirects its I/O to C2. In the first case, the interaction takes place in text mode via pipes. In the second case, Windows Console API operations are used, which allows attackers to fully emulate a console window on their side, taking into account information about the size of the screen buffer, cursor position, and other parameters.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">The configuration of the sample we examined contained the following set of strings:</p>

<h2 id="id4" class="break-words size_m__P_9U_ color_primary__z_39p margin_none__1sjaB">Conclusion</h2>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">APT groups with Asian roots continue to attack Russian companies, as evidenced by the activity of Space Pirates. Cybercriminals both develop new malware that implements non-standard techniques (such as Deed RAT) and use modifications of existing backdoors. Such modifications sometimes feature multiple layers of obfuscation to defeat security tools and complicate the analysis procedure—as in the case of BH_A006, built on the code of the popular Gh0st backdoor.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">A separate difficulty as regards APT groups operating out of the Asian region is accurate attribution: the frequent exchange of tools and, in some cases, joint activity of groups significantly complicate this task. The core part of our research is based on the results of our investigation of an information security incident at our client&#x27;s premises and analysis of specific network infrastructure that uses DDNS domains. The data obtained allows us to state with certainty that the same attackers are behind the detected activity.</p>
<p class="weight_regular__5MYqU size_l__TtckT margin_none__1sjaB color_secondary-plus__47VrA">PT ESC will continue to monitor the threats: new facts may provide more information about the activities of Space Pirates and its relationship with other groups.</p>

Center\"}]]}]\n2c:T541,\r\n\tAt the end of 2019, Positive Technologies Expert Security Center (PT ESC) found a phishing email aimed at a Russian aerospace enterprise. It contained a link to previously unknown malware. Our experts discovered the same malware in 2020 when investigating an information security incident at a Russian government agency. During the investigation, several new malware families using a common network infrastructure were also discovered, some of which had not previously been mentioned in open sources.\r\n\r\n\r\n\tIn the summer of 2021, PT ESC revealed traces of compromise of another Russian aerospace enterprise. The organization was duly informed. As a result of the investigation, we found connections to the same network infrastructure on its computers. Further research made it possible to identify at least two more organizations in Russia, both partially state-owned, that were attacked using the same malware and network infrastructure.\r\n\r\n\r\n\tWe could not unambiguously link the detected malicious activity to any known hacker group, so we gave the attackers a new name—Space Pirates. The reason for the name was the P1Rat string used in the PDB paths, and the targeting of the aerospace industry. This report describes the group's detected activity, the features of the malware it uses, as well as its connection with other APT
